<div class="sidebar-list mw-collapsible mw-collapsed"><div class="sidebar-list-title" style="background:#efefef;padding:0.2em;">Other themes</div><div class="sidebar-list-content mw-collapsible-content" style="padding-left:0.2em; padding-right:0.2em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Book_of_Discipline_(Quaker)" title="Book of Discipline (Quaker)"><i>Faith and Practice</i> or <i>Book of Discipline</i></a></li></ul>
<div class="hlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Clerk_(Quaker)" title="Clerk (Quaker)">Clerk</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Quaker_decision-making" class="mw-redirect" title="Quaker decision-making">Decision Making</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Quaker_businesses,_organizations_and_charities" title="List of Quaker businesses, organizations and charities">Businesses and charities</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Quakers" title="History of the Quakers">History</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Homosexuality_and_Quakerism" title="Homosexuality and Quakerism">Homosexuality</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Inward_light" title="Inward light">Inward light</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Friends_meeting_house" title="Friends meeting house">Meeting houses</a></li><li><a class="mw-selflink-fragment" href="#Quaker_teaching">Perfectionism</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Query_(Quaker)" title="Query (Quaker)">Query</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Friends_schools" title="List of Friends schools">Schools</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Quakers_in_science" title="Quakers in science">Science</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Quaker_Tapestry" title="Quaker Tapestry">Tapestry</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Quaker_wedding" title="Quaker wedding">Wedding</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Quaker_views_on_women" title="Quaker views on women">Women</a></li></ul></div></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below" style="padding-top:0.15em;">
<span class="noviewer" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:P_christianity.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/16px-P_christianity.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="14" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/24px-P_christianity.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/32px-P_christianity.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="360" /></a></span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Portal:Christianity" title="Portal:Christianity">Christianity&#32;portal</a></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349"><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Quakers_vertical" title="Template:Quakers vertical"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Quakers_vertical" title="Template talk:Quakers vertical"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Quakers_vertical&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><a href="/wiki/George_Fox" title="George Fox">George Fox</a>, the founder of <a href="/wiki/Quakerism" class="mw-redirect" title="Quakerism">Quakerism</a>, taught Christian perfection, also known in the Friends tradition as "perfectionism", in which the Christian believer could be made free from <a href="/wiki/Sin_in_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Sin in Christianity">sin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fox1661_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox1661-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stewart1992_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stewart1992-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In his <i>Some Principles of the Elect People of God Who in Scorn are called Quakers, for all the People throughout all Christendome to Read over, and thereby their own States to Consider</i>, he writes in section "XVI. Concerning Perfection":<sup id="cite_ref-Fox1661_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox1661-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>HE that hath brought Man into Imperfection is the Devil, and his work who led from God; for Man was Perfect before he fell, for all God's Works are Perfect; So Christ that destroyes the Devil and his works, makes man Perfect again, destroying him that made him Imperfect, which the Law could not do; so by his Blood doth he cleanse from all Sin; And by one offering, hath he Perfected for ever them that are Sanctified; And they that do not Believe in the Light which comes from Christ, by which they might see the Offering, and receive the Blood, are in the unbelief concerning this.
And the Apostles that were in the Light, Christ Jesus, (which destroyes the Devil and his works) spoke Wisdom among them that were Perfect, though they could not among those that were Carnal; And their Work was for the perfecting of the Saints, for that cause had they their Ministry given to them until they all came to the Knowledge of the Son of God, which doth destroy the Devil and his works, And which ends the Prophets, first Covenant, Types, Figures, Shadowes; And until they all came to the Unity of the Faith which purified their hearts, which gave them Victory over that which separated&#32;&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>&#93; from God, In which they had access to God, by which Faith they pleased him, by which they were Justified; And so until they came unto a Perfect Man, unto the Measure of the Stature of the fulness of Christ; and so the Apostle said, Christ in you we Preach the hope of Glory, warning every man, that we might present every Man Perfect in Christ Jesus.<sup id="cite_ref-Fox1661_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox1661-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The early Quakers, following Fox, taught that as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Born_again" title="Born again">New Birth</a> through the power of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Spirit" title="Holy Spirit">Holy Spirit</a>, man could be free from actual sinning if he continued to rely on the <a href="/wiki/Inward_light" title="Inward light">inward light</a> and "focus on the cross of Christ as the center of faith".<sup id="cite_ref-Elwell2001_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elwell2001-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> George Fox emphasized "personal responsibility for faith and emancipation from sin" in his teaching on perfectionism.<sup id="cite_ref-Elwell2001_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elwell2001-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> For the Christian, "perfectionism and freedom from sin were possible in this world".<sup id="cite_ref-Stewart1992_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stewart1992-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This traditional Quaker teaching continues to be emphasized by <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Friends" title="Conservative Friends">Conservative Friends</a>, such as the Ohio Yearly Meeting of the Religious Society of Friends and Holiness Friends, such as the <a href="/wiki/Central_Yearly_Meeting_of_Friends" title="Central Yearly Meeting of Friends">Central Yearly Meeting of Friends</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-OYM2022_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OYM2022-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CYMF2013_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CYMF2013-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Keswickian_teaching">Keswickian teaching</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_perfection&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Keswickian teaching">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Keswickian_theology" class="mw-redirect" title="Keswickian theology">Keswickian theology</a> teaches a second work of grace that occurs through "surrender and faith", in which God keeps an individual from sin.<sup id="cite_ref-Naselli_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naselli-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Keswickian denominations, such as the <a href="/wiki/Christian_and_Missionary_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian and Missionary Alliance">Christian and Missionary Alliance</a>, differ from the <a href="/wiki/Holiness_movement" title="Holiness movement">Wesleyan-Holiness movement</a> in that the Christian and Missionary Alliance does not see <a href="/wiki/Entire_sanctification" class="mw-redirect" title="Entire sanctification">entire sanctification</a> as cleansing one from <a href="/wiki/Original_sin" title="Original sin">original sin</a>, whereas holiness denominations espousing the <a href="/wiki/Wesleyan%E2%80%93Arminian_theology" class="mw-redirect" title="Wesleyan–Arminian theology">Wesleyan–Arminian theology</a> affirm this belief.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;B&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wu2012_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wu2012-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_perfection&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are Protestant denominations that reject the possibility of Christian perfection. Lutherans, citing letters by <a href="/wiki/Paul_of_Tarsus" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul of Tarsus">Paul of Tarsus</a> in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bible.oremus.org/?passage=Romans%207:14–25&amp;version=nrsv">Romans 7:14–25</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bible.oremus.org/?passage=Philippians%203:12&amp;version=nrsv">Philippians 3:12</a>, believe that "although we will strive for Christian perfection, we will not attain it in this life".<sup id="cite_ref-WELS-AOG_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WELS-AOG-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Modern apologists further note that:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Our <a href="/wiki/Salvation_(Christianity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvation (Christianity)">salvation</a> is complete and is simply received by faith. Good works are the fruit of that faith. Good works show that we are saved, but have no part in saving us. Becoming more and more God-like in this life is the result of being saved. If we are saved by becoming more and more God-like, our salvation is in doubt because our being God-like is never perfect in this life. The troubled conscience will find little comfort in an incomplete process of theosis, but will find much comfort in God's declaration of full and free forgiveness.<sup id="cite_ref-WELS-JS_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WELS-JS-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>While Presbyterians believe that Christians do "grow in God's grace" or holiness as they become conformed to the image of Christ, they reject the notion that perfection is attainable. In their view, sin will continue to affect one's motives and actions. This means that perfection is only attainable in <a href="/wiki/Glorification" title="Glorification">glorification</a> after death.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKim200388–89_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKim200388–89-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-96">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Though the <a href="/wiki/Christian_and_Missionary_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian and Missionary Alliance">Christian and Missionary Alliance</a> is characterized as <a href="/wiki/Keswickian" class="mw-redirect" title="Keswickian">Keswickian</a> in theology,<sup id="cite_ref-Kenyon2019_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenyon2019-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Knight2014_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight2014-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Murphy2018_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy2018-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BurgessMaas2010_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BurgessMaas2010-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> it departs from traditional Keswickian views on progressive <a href="/wiki/Sanctification" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanctification">sanctification</a> and by its rejection of suppressionism.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Knight2014_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight2014-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-Spirago-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Spirago_3-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Spirago_3-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFSpirago1899" class="citation book cs1">Spirago, Francis (1899). <i>The Catechism Explained</i>. Benziger Brothers. p.&#160;508. <q>1. God requires of all the just that they should aspire to Christian perfection. God desires the sinner to be converted, the just to strive after perfection. The duty of aspiring after perfection is included in the precept of charity, for it requires us to love God with all our strength. And what else does that mean but continual advancement in the path of virtue? "He that is just let him be justified still, and he that is holy let him be sanctified still"  (Apoc. xxii. 11). Our Lord lays this injunction upon  us: "Be you therefore perfect, as also your heavenly Father is perfect" (Matt. v. 48). The will of God is none other than our sanctification. He who does not aim at the attainment of  Christian perfection, is in danger of losing his soul. The vessel that does not stem the stream will drift downwards. Where there is no progression there is retrogression; no man can stand still on the path of virtue." As  soon," says St. Augustine," as thou art content with thyself, and thinkest thou hast done enough, thou art lost." We should aim at the highest degree of sanctity, imitating the trader, who is wont to ask the highest possible price for his wares.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Catechism+Explained&amp;rft.pages=508&amp;rft.pub=Benziger+Brothers&amp;rft.date=1899&amp;rft.aulast=Spirago&amp;rft.aufirst=Francis&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Jannakos2009-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Jannakos2009_4-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Jannakos2009_4-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Jannakos2009_4-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFJannakos2009" class="citation web cs1">Jannakos, Paul (2 October 2009). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.pravmir.com/is-human-perfection-possible/">"Is Human Perfection Possible?"</a>. Pravmir<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">6 December</span> 2021</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Is+Human+Perfection+Possible%3F&amp;rft.pub=Pravmir&amp;rft.date=2009-10-02&amp;rft.aulast=Jannakos&amp;rft.aufirst=Paul&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.pravmir.com%2Fis-human-perfection-possible%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.methodist.org.uk/about-us/the-methodist-church/what-is-distinctive-about-methodism/living-a-holy-life/">"Living a holy life"</a>. <i>methodist.org.uk</i>. <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church_of_Great_Britain" title="Methodist Church of Great Britain">Methodist Church of Great Britain</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">7 January</span> 2020</span>. <q>John Wesley taught about 'Christian perfection.' He believed that a mature Christian could reach a state where the love of God reigns supreme in our heart.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=methodist.org.uk&amp;rft.atitle=Living+a+holy+life&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.methodist.org.uk%2Fabout-us%2Fthe-methodist-church%2Fwhat-is-distinctive-about-methodism%2Fliving-a-holy-life%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Ogden2008-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Ogden2008_6-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Ogden2008_6-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFOden2008" class="citation book cs1"><a href="/wiki/Thomas_C._Oden" title="Thomas C. Oden">Oden, Thomas C.</a> (2008). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=XOZOacqHCx4C&amp;pg=PA190"><i>Doctrinal Standards in the Wesleyan Tradition: Revised Edition</i></a>. Abingdon Press. p.&#160;190. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4267-6124-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4267-6124-9"><bdi>978-1-4267-6124-9</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Doctrinal+Standards+in+the+Wesleyan+Tradition%3A+Revised+Edition&amp;rft.pages=190&amp;rft.pub=Abingdon+Press&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4267-6124-9&amp;rft.aulast=Oden&amp;rft.aufirst=Thomas+C.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DXOZOacqHCx4C%26pg%3DPA190&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-OYM2022-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-OYM2022_7-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-OYM2022_7-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.conservativefriend.org/perfectionfaq.htm">"An Evangelical Christian asks questions about sinlessness and perfection"</a>. Stillwater Monthly Meeting of Ohio Yearly Meeting of Friends<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">10 May</span> 2022</span>. <q>We are not justified by works. But good works follow necessarily as an indicator that we have accepted a relationship with Him through the application of our free will. If opening the door on which Jesus knocks is to be considered a work, then we are justified by works to that extent. But if we look at it as an obligation which we force on God--that is, if we believe that our good works are the agent of our salvation--then we miss the mark. The key is that God offers us the opportunity to become a genuine traveler in His company. Over time, if we do not resist it, the Light makes changes in us that bring us more and more into accordance with God's plans for us--we become more and more like what He wanted us to be. Over time, we sin less and less, as we become more and more in tune with His will. How clean a state of sinlessness is enough is not up to us--that decision belongs to Jesus. And providentially for us, Jesus is a merciful and compassionate judge. Quakers believe that we are called to be perfect, as our Father in Heaven is perfect. We are called to live a life as free of sin as we can. We believe that if God wants to bring a Christian to a state of sinless perfection, then He has that right and that power. We do not limit the power of the Holy Spirit in that matter.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=An+Evangelical+Christian+asks+questions+about+sinlessness+and+perfection&amp;rft.pub=Stillwater+Monthly+Meeting+of+Ohio+Yearly+Meeting+of+Friends&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.conservativefriend.org%2Fperfectionfaq.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Fox1661-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Fox1661_8-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Fox1661_8-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Fox1661_8-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Fox1661_8-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFGeorge_Fox1661" class="citation web cs1"><a href="/wiki/George_Fox" title="George Fox">George Fox</a> (1661). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.qhpress.org/texts/gfprinc.html#s16">"Some Principles of the Quakers"</a>. Robert Wilson.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Some+Principles+of+the+Quakers&amp;rft.pub=Robert+Wilson&amp;rft.date=1661&amp;rft.au=George+Fox&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.qhpress.org%2Ftexts%2Fgfprinc.html%23s16&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Against Heresies (Book IV, Chapter 39)</span>

<li id="cite_note-Burnett2006-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Burnett2006_12-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFBurnett2006" class="citation book cs1">Burnett, Daniel L. (15 March 2006). <i>In the Shadow of Aldersgate: An Introduction to the Heritage and Faith of the Wesleyan Tradition</i>. Wipf and Stock Publishers. pp.&#160;116–117. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-62189-980-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-62189-980-8"><bdi>978-1-62189-980-8</bdi></a>. <q>The doctrine of entire sanctification has been present from the very beginnings of the Christian faith. Since the focus of the first few centuries was on the battle against Christological heresies, a systematic doctrine of sanctification did not emerge during that period. Its roots, however, were clearly present in such Early Church Fathers as Irenaeus, Clement of Alexandria, and Origen. By the fourth century the highly regarded writings of Gregory of Nyssa and Macarius the Egyptian...advocated understandings of entire sanctification that sound very Wesleyan.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=In+the+Shadow+of+Aldersgate%3A+An+Introduction+to+the+Heritage+and+Faith+of+the+Wesleyan+Tradition&amp;rft.pages=116-117&amp;rft.pub=Wipf+and+Stock+Publishers&amp;rft.date=2006-03-15&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-62189-980-8&amp;rft.aulast=Burnett&amp;rft.aufirst=Daniel+L.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Winn-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Winn_58-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Winn_58-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFWinn2007" class="citation book cs1">Winn, Christian T. Wipf and Stock Publishers. p.&#160;115. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781630878320" title="Special:BookSources/9781630878320"><bdi>9781630878320</bdi></a>. <q>In addition to these separate denominational groupings, one needs to give attention to the large pockets of the Holiness movement that have remained within the United Methodist Church. The most influential of these would be the circles dominated by Asbury College and Asbury Theological Seminary (both in Wilmore, KY), but one could speak of other colleges, innumerable local campmeetings, the vestiges of various local Holiness associations, independent Holiness oriented missionary societies and the like that have had great impact within United Methodism. A similar pattern would exist in England with the role of Cliff College within Methodism in that context.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=From+the+Margins%3A+A+Celebration+of+the+Theological+Work+of+Donald+W.+Dayton&amp;rft.pages=115&amp;rft.pub=Wipf+and+Stock+Publishers&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.isbn=9781630878320&amp;rft.aulast=Winn&amp;rft.aufirst=Christian+T.+Collins&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Brown2011-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Brown2011_67-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Brown2011_67-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFBrown2011" class="citation web cs1">Brown, Allan (1 November 2011). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.gbs.edu/key-passages-that-teach-the-concept-of-entire-sanctification/">"Key Passages That Teach the Concept of Entire Sanctification"</a>. <a href="/wiki/God%27s_Bible_School_and_College" title="God&#39;s Bible School and College">God's Bible School and College</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">29 March</span> 2022</span>. <q>John Wesley observed in his Methodist Societies that wherever entire sanctification was not regularly preached and strongly urged upon Christians, believers grew cold and dead. In 1776, when he was 73 years of age, he wrote this to a friend: "Where Christian perfection [entire sanctification] is not strongly and explicitly preached, there is seldom any remarkable blessing from God; and consequently little addition to the society, and little life in the members of it. Speak and spare not. Let not regard for any man induce you to betray the truth of God. Till you press the believers to expect full salvation [entire sanctification] now, you must not look for any revival." (Works, Vol. 6, p.761).</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Key+Passages+That+Teach+the+Concept+of+Entire+Sanctification&amp;rft.pub=God%27s+Bible+School+and+College&amp;rft.date=2011-11-01&amp;rft.aulast=Brown&amp;rft.aufirst=Allan&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.gbs.edu%2Fkey-passages-that-teach-the-concept-of-entire-sanctification%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Synan2012-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Synan2012_78-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Synan2012_78-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Synan2012_78-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFSynan2012" class="citation book cs1">Synan, Vinson (30 January 2012). <i>The Century of the Holy Spirit: 100 Years of Pentecostal and Charismatic Renewal, 1901-2001</i>. Thomas Nelson. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4185-8753-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4185-8753-6"><bdi>978-1-4185-8753-6</bdi></a>. <q>Wesleyan Pentecostal Churches. ...Most of the first generation of Pentecostals were from this holiness stream that had its roots in Methodism. ...When the Pentecostal movement began, these "holiness Pentecostals" simply added the baptism in the Holy Spirit with tongues as "initial evidence" of a "third blessing" that brought power for witnessing to those who had already been sanctified. With the news tongues experience, sanctification was seen as a prerequisite "cleansing" that qualified the seeker to experience the "third blessing" of baptism in the Holy Spirit. An early prophetic utterance stated ominously that "My Spirit will not dwell in an unclean temple." Seekers were encouraged to abandon all the roots of bitterness and original sin so that nothing would block their reception of the Spirit. In fact, it was told that Seymour would not admit seekers to enter the upper room to seek the baptism until he was satisfied that their sanctification experience had been certified downstairs. The historic Azusa Street testimony was "I am saved, sanctified, and filled with the Holy Ghost."<span class="cs1-kern-right"></span></q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Century+of+the+Holy+Spirit%3A+100+Years+of+Pentecostal+and+Charismatic+Renewal%2C+1901-2001&amp;rft.pub=Thomas+Nelson&amp;rft.date=2012-01-30&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4185-8753-6&amp;rft.aulast=Synan&amp;rft.aufirst=Vinson&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-79">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFBarrett1988" class="citation journal cs1">Barrett, David B. (July 1988). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/239693938801200303">"The Twentieth-Century Pentecostal/Charismatic Renewal in the Holy Spirit, with its Goal of World Evangelization"</a>. <i>International Bulletin of Missionary Research</i>. <b>12</b> (3): 119–129. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1177%2F239693938801200303">10.1177/239693938801200303</a>. <a href="/wiki/ISSN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISSN (identifier)">ISSN</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.worldcat.org/issn/0272-6122">0272-6122</a>. <a href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:149417223">149417223</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=International+Bulletin+of+Missionary+Research&amp;rft.atitle=The+Twentieth-Century+Pentecostal%2FCharismatic+Renewal+in+the+Holy+Spirit%2C+with+its+Goal+of+World+Evangelization&amp;rft.volume=12&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.pages=119-129&amp;rft.date=1988-07&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A149417223%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft.issn=0272-6122&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1177%2F239693938801200303&amp;rft.aulast=Barrett&amp;rft.aufirst=David+B.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fjournals.sagepub.com%2Fdoi%2F10.1177%2F239693938801200303&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-80">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFKurianLamport2016" class="citation book cs1">Kurian, George Thomas; Lamport, Mark A. (10 November 2016). <i>Encyclopedia of Christianity in the United States</i>. Rowman &amp; Littlefield. p.&#160;1067. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4422-4432-0" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4422-4432-0"><bdi>978-1-4422-4432-0</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclopedia+of+Christianity+in+the+United+States&amp;rft.pages=1067&amp;rft.pub=Rowman+%26+Littlefield&amp;rft.date=2016-11-10&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4422-4432-0&amp;rft.aulast=Kurian&amp;rft.aufirst=George+Thomas&amp;rft.au=Lamport%2C+Mark+A.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-82">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">James Leo Garrett, <i>Systematic Theology, Volume 2, Second Edition</i>, Wipf and Stock Publishers, USA, 2014, p. 395; "Those branches of the Pentecostal movement in the United States which arose from the Holiness movement have retained the Wesleyan doctrine of entire sanctification and made baptism in or with the Spirit to be the third essential experience (e.g., Church of God, Cleveland, Tenn., Pentecostal Holiness Church, and Church of God in Christ)."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Anderson2004-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Anderson2004_83-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFAnderson2004" class="citation book cs1">Anderson, Allan (13 May 2004). <i>An Introduction to Pentecostalism: Global Charismatic Christianity</i>. Cambridge University Press. p.&#160;47. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-53280-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-53280-8"><bdi>978-0-521-53280-8</bdi></a>. <q>Those who resisted Durham's teaching and remained in the 'three-stage' camp were Seymour, Crawford and Parham, and Bishops Charles H. Mason, A.J. Tomlinson and J.H. King, respectively leaders of the Church of God in Christ, the Church of God (Cleveland) and the Pentecostal Holiness Church. Tomlinson and King each issued tirades against the 'finished work' doctrine in their periodicals, but by 1914 some 60 percent of all North American Pentecostals had embraced Durham's position. ... The 'Finished Work' controversy was only the first of many subsequent divisions in North American Pentecostalism. Not only did Pentecostal churches split over the question of sanctification as a distinct experience, but a more fundamental and acrimonious split erupted in 1916 over the doctrine of the Trinity. ... The 'New Issue' was a schism in the ranks of the 'Finished Work' Pentecostals that began as a teaching that the correct formula for baptism is 'in the name of Jesus' and developed into a dispute about the Trinity. It confirmed for Holiness Pentecostals that they should have no further fellowship with the 'Finished Work' Pentecostals, who were in 'heresy'.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=An+Introduction+to+Pentecostalism%3A+Global+Charismatic+Christianity&amp;rft.pages=47&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2004-05-13&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-53280-8&amp;rft.aulast=Anderson&amp;rft.aufirst=Allan&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFScott2006" class="citation web cs1">Scott, Rebekah (5 January 2006). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.post-gazette.com/local/westmoreland/2006/01/05/Murrysville-Bible-school-produces-teachers-preachers-prophets-and-apostles/stories/200601050316">"Murrysville Bible school produces teachers, preachers, prophets and apostles"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Post-Gazette" title="Pittsburgh Post-Gazette">Pittsburgh Post-Gazette</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">17 June</span> 2022</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Murrysville+Bible+school+produces+teachers%2C+preachers%2C+prophets+and+apostles&amp;rft.pub=Pittsburgh+Post-Gazette&amp;rft.date=2006-01-05&amp;rft.aulast=Scott&amp;rft.aufirst=Rebekah&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.post-gazette.com%2Flocal%2Fwestmoreland%2F2006%2F01%2F05%2FMurrysville-Bible-school-produces-teachers-preachers-prophets-and-apostles%2Fstories%2F200601050316&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Levinson1996-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Levinson1996_85-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFLevinson1996" class="citation book cs1">Levinson, David (1996). <i>Religion: A Cross-cultural Encyclopedia</i>. ABC-CLIO. p.&#160;151. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-87436-865-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-87436-865-9"><bdi>978-0-87436-865-9</bdi></a>. <q>The Finished Work Pentecostals believed that conversion and sanctification were a single act of grace. The Assemblies of God, created in 1914, became the first Finished Work denomination.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Religion%3A+A+Cross-cultural+Encyclopedia&amp;rft.pages=151&amp;rft.pub=ABC-CLIO&amp;rft.date=1996&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-87436-865-9&amp;rft.aulast=Levinson&amp;rft.aufirst=David&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Stewart1992-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Stewart1992_86-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Stewart1992_86-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFStewart1992" class="citation book cs1">Stewart, Kathleen Anne (1992). <i>The York Retreat in the Light of the Quaker Way: Moral Treatment Theory&#160;: Humane Therapy Or Mind Control?</i>. William Sessions. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781850720898" title="Special:BookSources/9781850720898"><bdi>9781850720898</bdi></a>. <q>On the other hand, Fox believed that perfectionism and freedom from sin were possible in this world.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+York+Retreat+in+the+Light+of+the+Quaker+Way%3A+Moral+Treatment+Theory+%3A+Humane+Therapy+Or+Mind+Control%3F&amp;rft.pub=William+Sessions&amp;rft.date=1992&amp;rft.isbn=9781850720898&amp;rft.aulast=Stewart&amp;rft.aufirst=Kathleen+Anne&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Kenyon2019-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Kenyon2019_90-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFKenyon2019" class="citation book cs1">Kenyon, Howard N. Simpson's Christian and Missionary Alliance, itself an ecumenical missionary movement</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Ethics+in+the+Age+of+the+Spirit%3A+Race%2C+Women%2C+War%2C+and+the+Assemblies+of+God&amp;rft.pub=Wipf+and+Stock+Publishers&amp;rft.date=2019-10-29&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4982-8522-3&amp;rft.aulast=Kenyon&amp;rft.aufirst=Howard+N.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Knight2014-91"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Knight2014_91-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Knight2014_91-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFIII2014" class="citation book cs1">III, Henry H. Knight (1 February 2014). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=UDpJAwAAQBAJ&amp;q=Christian+Missionary+Alliance+distinct+Wesleyan&amp;pg=PA91"><i>Anticipating Heaven Below: Optimism of Grace from Wesley to the Pentecostals</i></a>. Wipf and Stock Publishers. pp.&#160;91–92. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-63087-125-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-63087-125-3"><bdi>978-1-63087-125-3</bdi></a>. <q>It is the other christological strand, that of the indwelling Christ, that is the heart of the distinctive sanctification theology of A. B. Simpson. A Presbyterian who ultimately founded the Christian and Missionary Alliance, Simpson operates within a Keswick framework while also drawing upon Wesleyan ideals. Like Wesley, Simpson described sin as in the motive or intent of the heart most especially lack of love for God and neighbour. While he agrees with Keswick that we can't ever be freed from this sinful nature in this life, he insisted, as Van De Walle puts it, "the power of the resurrected Christ would more than enable the believer to consider the sin nature a vanquished foe and to behave as though it were.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Anticipating+Heaven+Below%3A+Optimism+of+Grace+from+Wesley+to+the+Pentecostals&amp;rft.pages=91-92&amp;rft.pub=Wipf+and+Stock+Publishers&amp;rft.date=2014-02-01&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-63087-125-3&amp;rft.aulast=III&amp;rft.aufirst=Henry+H.+Knight&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DUDpJAwAAQBAJ%26q%3DChristian%2BMissionary%2BAlliance%2Bdistinct%2BWesleyan%26pg%3DPA91&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Murphy2018-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Murphy2018_92-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFMurphy2018" class="citation book cs1">Murphy, Karen (23 May 2018). <i>Pentecostals and Roman Catholics on Becoming a Christian: Spirit-Baptism, Faith, Conversion, Experience, and Discipleship in Ecumenical Perspective</i>. <a href="/wiki/Brill_Academic_Publishers" class="mw-redirect" title="Brill Academic Publishers">Brill Academic Publishers</a>. p.&#160;131. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-90-04-36786-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-90-04-36786-9"><bdi>978-90-04-36786-9</bdi></a>. <q>... the Christian and Missionary Alliance (CMA) ... accepted the Keswickian teaching over the Wesleyan-Holiness belief.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Pentecostals+and+Roman+Catholics+on+Becoming+a+Christian%3A+Spirit-Baptism%2C+Faith%2C+Conversion%2C+Experience%2C+and+Discipleship+in+Ecumenical+Perspective&amp;rft.pages=131&amp;rft.pub=Brill+Academic+Publishers&amp;rft.date=2018-05-23&amp;rft.isbn=978-90-04-36786-9&amp;rft.aulast=Murphy&amp;rft.aufirst=Karen&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-BurgessMaas2010-93"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-BurgessMaas2010_93-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFBurgessMaas2010" class="citation book cs1">Burgess, Stanley M.; Maas, Eduard M. van der (3 August 2010). <i>The New International Dictionary of Pentecostal and Charismatic Movements: Revised and Expanded Edition</i>. Zondervan. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-310-87335-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-310-87335-8"><bdi>978-0-310-87335-8</bdi></a>. <q>A.B. Simpson, founder of the Christian and Missionary Alliance (CMA), influenced by A.J. Gordon and W.E. Boardman, adopted a Keswickian understanding of sanctification.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+New+International+Dictionary+of+Pentecostal+and+Charismatic+Movements%3A+Revised+and+Expanded+Edition&amp;rft.pub=Zondervan&amp;rft.date=2010-08-03&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-310-87335-8&amp;rft.aulast=Burgess&amp;rft.aufirst=Stanley+M.&amp;rft.au=Maas%2C+Eduard+M.+van+der&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+perfection" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-94"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-94">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Bernie A. Van De Walle, <i>The Heart of the Gospel: A. B. Simpson, the Fourfold Gospel, and Late Nineteenth-Century Evangelical Theology</i>, Wipf and Stock Publishers, USA, 2009, p. 93: "Despite similarities, Simpson's sanctification doctrine included its own distinctives, not duplicating either Keswick or Holiness soteriology", p. 94&#160;: "Richard Gilbertson, like McGraw, distinguishes between Simpson's view of sanctification and those of Keswick and Wesleyanism: There have been frequent attempts to categorize Simpson and the C&amp;MA. Often the assertion is made that Simpson held to a Keswick-type view of sanctification. More precisely, Simpson should be seen as having been influenced by Boardman's Higher Christian Life, a book which also impacted the Keswick movement. Other than an 1885 invitation to speak at one of their conferences, Simpson had little formal contact with the British Keswick movement.", p. 99: "Nevertheless, Simpson still held to a progressive understanding of sanctification, whereas Palmer believed that sanctification is received in some kind of terminal and complete form."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-95"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-95">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Gordon T. Smith, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://awf.world/consult/gordon-t-smith-conversion-and-sanctification-in-the-christian-and-missionary-alliance/">Conversion and Sanctification in the Christian &amp; Missionary Alliance</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20200109073433/http://awf.world/consult/gordon-t-smith-conversion-and-sanctification-in-the-christian-and-missionary-alliance/">Archived</a> 2020-01-09 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>, awf.world, Brazil, 1992&#160;: "He differed in some notable ways from the teachings of his contemporaries: he rejected the perfectionism of the Wesleyan-methodists; he did not accept the suppressionism of the Keswick movement." And "In these respects, the C&amp;MA is distinct from the Keswick movement. The Alliance heritage is more life and work affirming. Our actions in the world do make a difference and are meaningful."</span>
</li>
